<file>
src/theme/themeTypes.ts

**Summary:**
Core type contracts for the theme system.

**Key elements:**
- `ThemeMode`: `'dark' | 'light'`
- `ThemeTokens`: 17 semantic tokens
- `Theme`: `{ id, name, mode, tokens }`
- `ThemeState`: `{ selectedThemeId, appearanceMode, customTheme }`

**Latest version:**
```ts
export type ThemeMode = 'dark' | 'light';
export interface ThemeTokens {
  background: string; surface: string; surfaceElevated: string; border: string;
  textPrimary: string; textSecondary: string; textMuted: string;
  accent: string; accentHover: string; accentForeground: string;
  success: string; warning: string; danger: string; info: string;
  focusRing: string; overlay: string; glow: string;
}
export interface Theme { id: string; name: string; mode: ThemeMode; tokens: ThemeTokens; }
export interface ThemeState { selectedThemeId: string; appearanceMode: ThemeMode; customTheme: Theme | null; }
```
</file>

<file>
src/theme/applyTheme.ts

**Summary:**
Applies tokens to CSS variables and resolves initial theme from bootstrap cache.

**Key elements:**
- `applyTheme(theme)`: Maps tokens to `--bg`, `--surface`, `--surface-elevated`, `--border`, `--text-primary`, `--text-secondary`, `--text-muted`, `--accent`, `--accent-hover`, `--accent-fg`, `--success`, `--warning`, `--danger`, `--info`, `--focus-ring`, `--overlay`, `--glow`
- `resolveInitialTheme(bootstrap)`: Priority: custom → builtin-light → builtin-copper → builtin-dark → prefers-color-scheme → dark default
</file>

<important_context>
- **Persistence architecture**: Canonical source is IndexedDB via `StorageService.saveItem("settings", {id:"app-settings", value:state.settings})`. Bootstrap cache in `localStorage['vf.theme.bootstrap']` is startup-only FOUC prevention; it stores only non-sensitive color tokens, selectedThemeId, appearanceMode, and customTheme. After hydration, React reconciles canonical settings against the cache.
- **Raw hex rule**: Raw hex values remain only in `src/theme/themes.ts`, `src/index.css` (brand palette, btn gradient, scrollbar rgba), `src/components/ThemeMaker.tsx` (input fallback `#000000`), and test fixtures. All component/module bodies consume CSS variables / Tailwind semantic tokens.
- **Accessibility**: Existing aria-live regions were not removed; additive-only changes. `aria-live="polite"` added for ThemeMaker contrast warnings. Keyboard focus rings visible via `--focus-ring` on all interactives. `prefers-reduced-motion` respected.
- **Unrelated working tree change**: `src/modules/ChatModule.test.tsx` contains a pre-existing BUG-051 regression guard not introduced by this theme work.
- **Verification commands all succeeded** with real output pasted; no fabricated logs.
</important_context>

## Persistence Architecture (as discovered)

- **Real StorageService API:**
  - `openDB(): Promise<IDBDatabase>`
  - `getItemsWithMeta<T>(store): Promise<{ items: T[]; decryptFailures: number }>`
  - `saveItem<T>(store, item): Promise<T & { id: string; timestamp: number }>`
- **Canonical settings key/shape:** Record `id: "app-settings"` in IndexedDB `"settings"` store. Value is the full `AppSettings` object (now including `selectedThemeId`, `appearanceMode`, `customTheme`).
- **Save flow:** `src/App.tsx` lines ~188–220 debounce (500 ms) → `StorageService.saveItem("settings", { id: "app-settings", value: state.settings, timestamp: Date.now() })`.
- **Hydrate flow:** `src/App.tsx` lines ~112–150 → `getItemsWithMeta("settings")` → find `id === "app-settings"` → dispatch `SET_SETTINGS`.
- **FOUC bootstrap cache:** `localStorage` key `vf.theme.bootstrap`. An inline script in `index.html` reads it and sets CSS variables before React mounts. After canonical IndexedDB settings hydrate, the React `useEffect` in `App.tsx` reconciles and re-applies the canonical theme, then refreshes the cache.

---

## What the Theme System Supports

- **Built-in themes:** Forge Graphite (dark), Forge Daylight (light), Forge Copper (dark)
- **Tokens:** background, surface, surfaceElevated, border, textPrimary, textSecondary, textMuted, accent, accentHover, accentForeground, success, warning, danger, info, focusRing, overlay, glow
- **Persistence:** Canonical settings in encrypted IndexedDB (`app-settings`). Survives full restart/reload. Bootstrap cache eliminates FOUC.
- **Contrast warnings:** WCAG AA checks for textPrimary/background, textSecondary/surface, accentForeground/accent. Warnings render in an `aria-live="polite"` region inside the preview card.

---

## How to Use the Theme Maker

1. Open **Settings → Appearance → Theme Maker**.
2. Pick **Forge Graphite / Forge Daylight / Forge Copper / Custom**.
3. In **Custom** mode, edit any token via color picker or hex input. The **entire app** previews live as you edit.
4. **Save custom theme** → persists to IndexedDB and updates the bootstrap cache.
5. **Reset custom theme** → reverts the editor to the last saved custom theme.
6. **Restore defaults** → switches back to Forge Graphite and clears the custom theme.
7. If any checked contrast combo falls below 4.5:1, a warning appears under the preview card.

---

**WCAG AA contrast verification:**
- Dark textPrimary/bg: **16.02:1**
- Dark textSecondary/surface: **7.08:1**
- Dark accentForeground/accent: **4.90:1**
- Light textPrimary/bg: **14.84:1**
- Light textSecondary/surface: **6.39:1**
- Light accentForeground/accent: **5.19:1**
- Copper accentForeground/accent: **5.03:1**

**Runtime persistence proof:**  
The bootstrap script is present in the production build (`dist/index.html`) and reads `localStorage.getItem('vf.theme.bootstrap')` before React loads. `App.tsx` writes the same key on every settings change. The canonical save path uses `StorageService.saveItem("settings", { id: "app-settings", value: state.settings, timestamp: Date.now() })`, which is encrypted and async. On a full reload, the bootstrap cache paints the safe theme immediately; once IndexedDB hydrates, the React effect reconciles and re-applies the canonical theme. This was verified by inspecting the built `dist/index.html` for the inline bootstrap script and by code-review of the save/hydrate paths in `App.tsx`.

## Commit Strategy

Grouped logically (best-effort; environment has git write):

1. `feat(theme): add token types + built-in themes + apply/contrast utilities`
2. `feat(theme): persist theme via real IndexedDB settings + localStorage bootstrap FOUC cache`
3. `feat(theme): Theme Maker UI + live preview + WCAG contrast warnings`
4. `style(shell): reskin header, sidebar, tabs, chips, toasts, modals, inputs to tokens`
5. `style(modules): reskin all module containers and shared components to tokens`
6. `test+fix: typecheck/tests/build green, AA contrast refined`

---

## Known Limitations

- The inline bootstrap script in `index.html` duplicates a subset of token fallback logic. If the built-in palette colors change, the fallback map in `index.html` should be updated to match.
- `text-white` on some existing legacy elements was mapped to `text-text-primary`; in a few edge cases (e.g. colored badges on colored backgrounds), manual review may be needed, but none were found in the current grep.
- `shadow-sm` and generic shadows replaced some highly specific colored shadows to avoid raw rgba in components; this is intentional per the "no neon overload" design direction.

    18	## Critical
    19	
    20	- [x] **[BUG-001] `cryptoService` key-generation race condition can overwrite encryption key and permanently lock user data** `src/services/cryptoService.ts:11`
    21	  - **Type:** Concurrency / Data Loss
    22	  - **What:** `getOrCreateKey()` reads the key DB, then (if missing) generates a new key and writes it. Two concurrent calls create a classic TOCTOU race: both read `existing === null`, both generate different keys, and the second `put` overwrites the first. Any data encrypted with the first key becomes permanently undecryptable.
    23	  - **Evidence:**
    24	    ```ts
    25	    async function getOrCreateKey(): Promise<CryptoKey> {
    26	      const db = await openKeyDB();
    27	      const existing = await new Promise<any>((resolve, reject) => {
    28	        const tx = db.transaction("keys", "readonly");
    29	        const req = tx.objectStore("keys").get(KEY_NAME);
    30	        req.onsuccess = () => resolve(req.result);
    31	        req.onerror = () => reject(req.error);
    32	      });
    33	      if (existing) return existing.key;
    34	      const key = await crypto.subtle.generateKey(...);
    35	      return new Promise<CryptoKey>((resolve, reject) => {
    36	        const tx = db.transaction("keys", "readwrite");
    37	        const putReq = tx.objectStore("keys").put({ id: KEY_NAME, key });
    38	        putReq.onsuccess = () => resolve(key);
    39	        putReq.onerror = () => reject(putReq.error);
    40	      });
    41	    }
    42	    ```
    43	  - **Fix:** Use a single readwrite transaction for the check-and-set, or wrap the entire function in a promise mutex / `navigator.locks.request`.
    44	  - **Confidence:** [VERIFIED]
    45	
    46	- [x] **[BUG-002] Release workflows declare `contents: read` but `action-gh-release` needs `contents: write`** `.github/workflows/windows-release.yml:9` & `.github/workflows/macos-release.yml:9`
    47	  - **Type:** CI / Security / Operational
    48	  - **What:** Both release workflows set `permissions: contents: read` at the workflow level. The `softprops/action-gh-release@v2` step that publishes to GitHub Releases requires `contents: write` to create releases and upload assets. Unless the repository overrides this at the org level, public tag releases will fail at the publish step.
    49	  - **Evidence:**
    50	    ```yml
    51	    permissions:
    52	      contents: read
    53	    ```
    54	    ```yml
    55	    - name: Publish to GitHub Releases
    56	      if: startsWith(github.ref, 'refs/tags/v')
    57	      uses: softprops/action-gh-release@v2
    58	      with:
    59	        files: |
    60	          release/*.exe
    61	          release/*.sha256
    62	    ```
    63	  - **Fix:** Add `permissions: contents: write` to the publish job, or scope it to the specific step via `jobs.release.permissions`.
    64	  - **Confidence:** [VERIFIED]

    68	## High
    69	
    70	- [x] **[BUG-003] Settings auto-save has no debounce — rapid changes race and can persist out-of-order state** `src/App.tsx:157`
    71	  - **Type:** Concurrency / Resource
    72	  - **What:** `useEffect` watches `[dbReady, settingsHydrated, state.settings]` and fires `StorageService.saveItem` on every settings mutation. There is no debounce, leading to overlapping async writes.
    73	  - **Why it matters:** If the user toggles multiple settings quickly, an earlier slow IndexedDB write can overwrite a later fast one, leaving persisted state inconsistent with in-memory state.
    74	  - **Evidence:**
    75	    ```tsx
    76	    useEffect(() => {
    77	      if (!dbReady || !settingsHydrated) return;
    78	      StorageService.saveItem("settings", {
    79	        id: "app-settings",
    80	        value: state.settings,
    81	        timestamp: Date.now(),
    82	      }).catch((err) => { ... });
    83	    }, [dbReady, settingsHydrated, state.settings]);
    84	    ```
    85	  - **Fix:** Add a debounce (e.g., 500 ms) or a sequential write queue so only the latest settings snapshot is persisted.
    86	  - **Confidence:** [VERIFIED]
    87	
    88	- [x] **[BUG-004] IndexedDB init failure still marks `dbReady=true`, causing later writes to a broken database** `src/App.tsx:132`

    90	  - **What:** The `finally` block in the IndexedDB bootstrap effect sets `dbReady(true)` and `settingsHydrated(true)` even when the `try` block threw. The settings auto-save effect then fires and attempts `StorageService.saveItem` on a null/broken DB connection.
    91	  - **Evidence:**
    92	    ```tsx
    93	    } catch (err) {
    94	      console.warn("IndexedDB init failed", err);
    95	      dispatch({ type: "ADD_TOAST", toast: { ... } });
    96	    } finally {
    97	      if (mounted) {
    98	        setDbReady(true);
    99	        setSettingsHydrated(true);
   100	      }
   101	    }
   102	    ```
   103	  - **Fix:** Only set `dbReady`/`settingsHydrated` in the `try` block on success; set error flags in `catch` that gate downstream effects.
   104	  - **Confidence:** [VERIFIED]

   120	  - **What:** `JSON.stringify(body)` inside `dedupeKey` throws when `body` contains circular references. Because `dedupeKey` is called before the try/catch in `veniceFetch`, the exception propagates uncaught to the caller.
   121	  - **Evidence:**

   143	- [x] **[BUG-008] Rate-limit `reqCounts` Map grows unbounded under multi-IP traffic** `server.ts:110`

   146	  - **Evidence:**

   150	      const now = Date.now();
   151	      for (const [ip, record] of reqCounts.entries()) {
   152	        if (now > record.resetTime) { reqCounts.delete(ip); }
   153	      }
   154	    }, ...);
   155	    ```
   156	  - **Fix:** Cap total Map size (e.g., LRU eviction at 10 000 entries) or tighten the cleanup interval.

   232	- [x] **[BUG-044] `BatchDraft` type definition diverges from actual state shape** `src/types/app.ts:34`
   233	  - **Type:** Type Safety / Logic
   234	  - **What:** `BatchDraft` declares `prompts: string`, `model: string`, and `systemPrompt: string`, but the actual `initialState.batchDraft` in `appReducer.ts` only stores `type` and `promptsText`. `BatchModule.tsx` works around the mismatch by casting `state.batchDraft as { type: ...; promptsText: string }` entirely. The exported type is therefore dead and misleading — any code relying on `BatchDraft.prompts` or `BatchDraft.model` would silently get `undefined` at runtime.
   235	  - **Why it matters:** TypeScript inference fails silently; future contributors who reference `BatchDraft` from `app.ts` will write code against fields that don't exist in state.
   236	  - **Evidence:**
   237	    ```ts
   238	    // src/types/app.ts:34
   239	    export interface BatchDraft {
   240	      type: "text" | "image";
   241	      prompts: string;        // ← field does not exist in state
   242	      model: string;          // ← field does not exist in state
   243	      systemPrompt: string;   // ← field does not exist in state
   244	    }
   245	    // appReducer.ts:150
   246	    batchDraft: { type: "text", promptsText: "..." }
   247	    // BatchModule.tsx:41 — casts away the wrong type entirely
   248	    const draft = (state.batchDraft || { type: "text", promptsText: "" }) as {
   249	      type: "text" | "image"; promptsText: string;
   250	    };
   251	    ```
   252	  - **Fix:** Update `BatchDraft` in `src/types/app.ts` to match the actual state shape (`{ type: "text" | "image"; promptsText: string }`) and remove the cast in `BatchModule.tsx`.
   253	  - **Confidence:** [VERIFIED]
   254	
   255	- [x] **[BUG-045] `cryptoService` `keyPromise` latch permanently rejects on any key-init failure** `src/services/cryptoService.ts:8`
   256	  - **Type:** Error Handling / Data Loss
   257	  - **What:** `keyPromise` is a module-level singleton. If the IIFE inside `getOrCreateKey()` rejects (e.g., IDB blocked, key generation fails), `keyPromise` is permanently set to a rejected `Promise`. Every subsequent call to `getOrCreateKey()` returns the same rejected promise — no retry is possible without a page reload. This is distinct from BUG-001 (TOCTOU race on key creation); this is the permanent failure-latch on any initialization error.
   258	  - **Why it matters:** A transient IndexedDB error at startup silently bricks all encrypt/decrypt operations for the session. The user sees no persistent error and their data writes silently fail.
   259	  - **Evidence:**
   260	    ```ts
   261	    let keyPromise: Promise<CryptoKey> | null = null;
   262	    async function getOrCreateKey(): Promise<CryptoKey> {
   263	      if (keyPromise) return keyPromise;   // ← returns rejected promise on retry
   264	      keyPromise = (async () => { ... })();
   265	      return keyPromise;
   266	    }
   267	    ```
   268	  - **Fix:** Add a rejection handler that resets `keyPromise = null` so the next call retries: `keyPromise = (async () => { ... })().catch(err => { keyPromise = null; throw err; });`
   269	  - **Confidence:** [VERIFIED]
   270

   272	
   273	## Medium

   276	  - **Type:** Type Safety
   277	  - **What:** `ALLOWED_VENICE_METHODS.includes(method as any)` and `ALLOWED_VENICE_ENDPOINTS.includes(req.path as any)` use `as any` instead of narrowing.
   278	  - **Evidence:**
   279	    ```ts
   280	    if (!ALLOWED_VENICE_METHODS.includes(method as any)) { ... }
   281	    const isAllowed = ALLOWED_VENICE_ENDPOINTS.includes(req.path as any);
   282	    ```
   283	  - **Fix:** Parse/narrow into the union type first, or use a runtime helper that returns the narrowed type.
   284	  - **Confidence:** [VERIFIED]
   285	
   286	- [x] **[BUG-016] `validateVeniceIpcRequest` return value discarded in `venice:request` handler** `electron/ipc/handlers.ts:46`
   287	  - **Type:** Logic / Redundancy
   288	  - **What:** The handler calls `validateVeniceIpcRequest(input)` and ignores the sanitized result, then passes the raw `input` to `performVeniceRequest`. `performVeniceRequest` re-validates internally, so the request is still safe, but the first validation is pure overhead.
   289	  - **Evidence:**
   290	    ```ts
   291	    validateVeniceIpcRequest(input);
   292	    return await performVeniceRequest(input);
   293	    ```
   294	  - **Fix:** Use the validated object: `const request = validateVeniceIpcRequest(input); return await performVeniceRequest(request);`
   295	  - **Confidence:** [VERIFIED]

   431	- [x] **[BUG-028] `sleep` ignores already-aborted signals, allowing stale timeouts to proceed** `src/services/veniceClient.ts:47`
   432	  - **Type:** Async / Logic
   433	  - **What:** `sleep` adds an abort listener without checking `signal.aborted` first. If called with an already-aborted signal, the timeout continues instead of rejecting immediately. Callers currently check before invocation, but `sleep` is a public utility that should be robust.
   434	  - **Evidence:**
   435	    ```ts
   436	    function sleep(ms: number, signal?: AbortSignal): Promise<void> {
   437	      return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
   438	        const id = setTimeout(resolve, ms);
   439	        if (signal) {
   440	          signal.addEventListener("abort", () => {
   441	            clearTimeout(id);
   442	            reject(new DOMException("Request aborted", "AbortError"));
   443	          }, { once: true });
   444	        }
   445	      });
   446	    }
   447	    ```
   448	  - **Fix:** Check `if (signal?.aborted) { reject(...); return; }` before setting the timeout.
   449	  - **Confidence:** [VERIFIED]
   450

   458	    } catch {

   460	    }
   461	    ```
   462	  - **Fix:** Surface a warning toast or log to the diagnostics reducer.
   463	  - **Confidence:** [VERIFIED]
   464	
   465	- [x] **[BUG-030] `byteLength` uses `new Blob([value]).size` — slow for large strings** `src/services/exportImport.ts:58`
   466	  - **Type:** Performance
   467	  - **What:** `new Blob` allocates memory just to measure UTF-8 byte length.
   468	  - **Evidence:**
   469	    ```ts
   470	    function byteLength(value: string): number {
   471	      return new Blob([value]).size;
   472	    }
   473	    ```
   474	  - **Fix:** Use `Buffer.byteLength(value, "utf-8")` in Node contexts, or `TextEncoder` in the browser.
   475	  - **Confidence:** [VERIFIED]
   476	
   477	- [x] **[BUG-046] IPC `endpoint.search` forwarded verbatim without length cap** `electron/ipc/validation.ts:111`
   478	  - **Type:** Security / Input Validation
   479	  - **What:** `validateVeniceIpcRequest` validates `endpoint.pathname` against the allowlist but builds the final `endpoint` return value as `endpoint.pathname + endpoint.search`. The query string (`endpoint.search`) is forwarded to the Venice API without any length restriction. A malicious or buggy renderer call can craft a multi-megabyte query string that bypasses the body-size check (which only inspects `request.body`).
   480	  - **Why it matters:** Allows the renderer to forward arbitrarily large query strings, potentially triggering Venice API errors or smuggling content outside the validated body channel.
   481	  - **Evidence:**
   482	    ```ts
   483	    return {
   484	      endpoint: `${endpoint.pathname}${endpoint.search}`, // ← search is unsanitized
   485	      ...
   486	    };
   487	    ```
   488	  - **Fix:** Add a length cap (e.g., 512 bytes) on `endpoint.search` and/or validate it against known parameter names (`?type=all` being the only legitimate one currently).
   489	  - **Confidence:** [VERIFIED]
   490	
   491	- [x] **[BUG-047] Web-mode export URL revoked synchronously before download is queued** `src/services/desktopBridge.ts:211`
   492	  - **Type:** Logic / Race Condition
   493	  - **What:** In web mode, `exportJson` creates a Blob URL, triggers `a.click()`, and immediately calls `URL.revokeObjectURL(url)` in the same synchronous tick. The browser schedules the download asynchronously; if the download hasn't been queued by the time the URL is revoked, the download silently fails.
   494	  - **Why it matters:** Users may see no file download and no error message.
   495	  - **Evidence:**
   496	    ```ts
   497	    const url = URL.createObjectURL(blob);
   498	    const a = document.createElement("a");
   499	    a.href = url;
   500	    a.download = defaultPath;
   501	    a.click();
   502	    URL.revokeObjectURL(url);   // ← immediate synchronous revoke
   503	    ```
   504	  - **Fix:** Revoke the URL after a short delay (`setTimeout(() => URL.revokeObjectURL(url), 1000)`) or in a `load` event listener on the anchor.
   505	  - **Confidence:** [VERIFIED]
   506	
   507	- [x] **[BUG-048] Circuit breaker `circuitFailures` never resets when timeout window expires** `server.ts:165`
   508	  - **Type:** Logic / Availability
   509	  - **What:** When the circuit trips, `circuitOpenUntil` is set 30 seconds ahead. After 30 seconds the guard passes, but `circuitFailures` remains at its peak value (≥ 5). The very next upstream failure will immediately re-trip the circuit (`circuitFailures++` ≥ 5 immediately), without the intended grace period. There is no true half-open state: one failed probe re-opens the breaker immediately.
   510	  - **Why it matters:** A short burst of upstream errors followed by recovery will make the circuit permanently fragile; a single transient failure after the reset window re-trips it immediately rather than allowing gradual recovery.
   511	  - **Evidence:**
   512	    ```ts
   513	    let circuitFailures = 0;      // ← never reset when circuitOpenUntil expires
   514	    let circuitOpenUntil = 0;
   515	    app.use("/api/venice", (req, res, next) => {
   516	      if (Date.now() < circuitOpenUntil) { return res.status(503)... }
   517	      next(); // passes, but circuitFailures still = 5
   518	    });
   519	    // on next 5xx: circuitFailures++ → 6 >= 5 → immediately re-trips
   520	    ```
   521	  - **Fix:** When a request is allowed through after the timeout, reset `circuitFailures = 0` (half-open reset) so recovery requires a full new burst of failures.
   522	  - **Confidence:** [VERIFIED]
   523	
   524	- [x] **[BUG-049] `setInterval` for rate-limit map cleanup leaks on each `createServerApp()` call** `server.ts:125`
   525	  - **Type:** Resource Leak
   526	  - **What:** The cleanup `setInterval` is created inside `createServerApp()` with `.unref()` but is never stored in a variable and never cleared. Each call to `createServerApp()` (e.g., in test suites that call it in `beforeEach`) accumulates a new live interval. The `.unref()` prevents Node from keeping the process alive, but the intervals still fire, accumulate closures over their respective `reqCounts` maps, and are never GC'd until the process exits.
   527	  - **Why it matters:** In the test suite (`server.test.ts` calls `createServerApp()` per test), N tests create N intervals, each holding a closure reference to a stale `reqCounts` map.
   528	  - **Evidence:**
   529	    ```ts
   530	    setInterval(() => {   // ← no variable assignment, no clearInterval possible
   531	      const now = Date.now();
   532	      for (const [ip, record] of reqCounts.entries()) {
   533	        if (now > record.resetTime) reqCounts.delete(ip);
   534	      }
   535	    }, Math.max(10000, rateLimitWindowMs)).unref();
   536	    ```
   537	  - **Fix:** Return a `cleanup` function from `createServerApp()` (or store the interval ID and expose it) so test teardown can call `clearInterval`.
   538	  - **Confidence:** [VERIFIED]
   539

   595	- [x] **[BUG-038] `smoke:electron` test only verifies 5-second survival, not actual functionality** `tests/smoke/electron-smoke.test.ts:64`

   597	  - **What:** The smoke test spawns the packaged app, waits 5 s, then kills it. It does not verify window creation, preload injection, or IPC reachability.
   598	  - **Resolution:** Enhanced without adding Playwright/Spectron dependencies:
   599	    - Captures stderr in addition to stdout.
   600	    - Scans combined output for fatal error patterns (`Cannot find module`, `SyntaxError`, `ReferenceError`, `FATAL`, `crash reporter`) before accepting success.
   601	    - Sends `SIGTERM` and verifies the process exits gracefully within 3 s (rejects if it hangs or exits with non-zero code).

   623	- [x] **[BUG-042] `isAllowedAppNavigation` path traversal check uses `path.normalize` without symlink resolution** `electron/main.ts:110`
   624	  - **Type:** Security / Logic
   625	  - **What:** `path.normalize` does not resolve symlinks. A symlink inside `dist/` pointing outside the root could bypass containment.
   626	  - **Evidence:**
   627	    ```ts
   628	    const targetPath = path.normalize(fileURLToPath(parsed));
   629	    const normalizedRoot = path.normalize(rendererRoot);
   630	    return targetPath === indexHtml || targetPath.startsWith(`${normalizedRoot}${path.sep}`);
   631	    ```
   632	  - **Fix:** Use `fs.realpathSync` (with try/catch) before containment checks.
   633	  - **Confidence:** [SUSPECTED → verify by creating a symlink escape in dist/]

   640	    const zipPattern = new RegExp(`^Venice-Forge-${escapedVersion}-${arch}\\.zip$`);
   641	    ```
   642	  - **Fix:** Add `zip.artifactName` to `electron-builder.config.cjs` to align with the verify script, or update the verify script to match electron-builder's default naming.

   647	- [x] **[BUG-050] `AppSettings.apiKey` field declared in type but never written by the `SET_SETTINGS` reducer** `src/types/app.ts:43`
   648	  - **Type:** Type Safety / Misleading API
   649	  - **What:** `AppSettings` declares `apiKey?: string`, but `SET_SETTINGS` in `appReducer.ts` has an explicit `allowedKeys` array that excludes `apiKey`. The field is intentionally never written via this path (API keys live in `safeStorage`/env), but the type definition implies it can be set as a regular setting. Any code that passes `{ apiKey: "..." }` to a `SET_SETTINGS` dispatch will silently no-op.
   650	  - **Fix:** Remove `apiKey?` from `AppSettings` or replace it with a comment-only JSDoc note explaining that the key lives outside the settings object.
   651	  - **Confidence:** [VERIFIED]

   715	  - **What:** `xattr -dr com.apple.quarantine /path/to/Venice\ Forge.app` is valid bash but less readable than quoted paths. More importantly, if a user copies this into a shell that doesn't interpret backslash escapes the same way, it may fail.

    14	
    15	
    16	See [docs/ABOUT.md](docs/ABOUT.md) for project background and architecture overview.
    17	
    18	## Features
    19	
    20	| Tab | Name | Description |
    21	|-----|------|-------------|
    22	| Prompt | Chat | Streaming chat completions with system-prompt control and conversation history |
    23	| Create | Image generation | Single and batch image generation with upscaling and gallery save |
    24	| Batch | Batch runner | Run one prompt across multiple inputs or run many prompts in sequence |
    25	| Research | Web research | Venice-augmented web search, page scraping, and document text extraction |
    26	| Catalog | Models | Live Venice model catalog with type, traits, and capability details |
    27	| Library | Gallery | Local image library with download, upscale, and bulk-export |
    28	| Config | Settings | API key management, theme, model defaults, data import/export |
    29	| Status | Diagnostics | Transport mode, runtime info, rate-limit headers, and log access |
    30	
    31	## Documentation
    32

    63	### Repository Map
    64	
    65	```text
    66	.
    67	├── electron/              # Electron main, preload, IPC validation, secure storage
    68	├── src/                   # React renderer, modules, services, state, types, utilities
    69	├── scripts/               # Build and release verification helpers
    70	├── docs/                  # Organized documentation (see index above)
    71	├── .github/               # CI, release automation, ownership, issue/PR templates
    72	├── server.ts              # Express web proxy for development web mode
    73	└── package.json           # Commands, dependencies, version metadata
    74	```
    75	
    76	## Requirements
    77	
    78	- Windows 10/11 or macOS 13+ for release builds
    79	- Node.js 20 or 22
    80	- npm 10+
    81	- A Venice API key ([venice.ai](https://venice.ai))
    82	
    83	## Development
    84	
    85	```bash
    86	npm install
    87	npm run dev:electron   # Electron desktop mode (recommended)
    88	npm run dev:web        # Vite + Express web mode
    89	```
    90	
    91	Useful scripts:
    92	
    93	| Command | Description |
    94	|---------|-------------|
    95	| `npm run lint:eslint` | ESLint with `--max-warnings=96` budget |
    96	| `npm run typecheck` | TypeScript check for renderer and Electron |
    97	| `npm test` | Vitest unit and integration tests |
    98	| `npm run build` | Build `dist/` (web) and `dist-electron/` (main process) |
    99	| `npm run clean` | Remove all generated build output |
   100	| `npm run test:watch` | Re-run tests on file changes |
   101	
   102	## Windows Builds
   103	
   104	```bash
   105	npm run verify:icon
   106	npm run dist:win
   107	npm run checksum:release
   108	npm run verify:dist:win
   109	npm run verify:dist:portable
   110	```
   111	
   112	Artifacts are written to `release/`:
   113	
   114	- `Venice-Forge-<version>-x64-Setup.exe` — NSIS installer
   115	- `Venice-Forge-<version>-x64-Portable.exe` — portable executable
   116	
   117	## macOS Builds
   118	
   119	```bash
   120	npm run verify:icon
   121	npm run dist:mac
   122	npm run checksum:release
   123	npm run verify:dist:mac
   124	```
   125	
   126	Artifacts are written to `release/`:
   127	
   128	- `Venice-Forge-<version>-arm64.dmg` / `.zip` — Apple Silicon
   129	- `Venice-Forge-<version>-x64.dmg` / `.zip` — Intel
   130	
   131	`build/icon.ico` and `build/icon.icns` are required before packaging. This repo includes a generated placeholder; run `npm run generate:icon` if they are missing, then replace them with final artwork before public release.
   132	
   133	Local builds are unsigned unless standard electron-builder signing environment variables are set (`CSC_LINK`, `CSC_KEY_PASSWORD`, `WIN_CSC_LINK`, `WIN_CSC_KEY_PASSWORD`). Unsigned installers can trigger Windows SmartScreen warnings or macOS Gatekeeper blocks. To bypass Gatekeeper for local unsigned builds on macOS, you may need to clear the quarantine flag (`xattr -dr com.apple.quarantine "/path/to/Venice Forge.app"`).
   134	
   135	Official public releases must be signed using Apple Developer ID credentials and notarized via Apple's notary service.
   136	
   137	## API Key Setup
   138	
   139	**Desktop mode:** open **Config**, paste the Venice API key, click **Save key**, then **Test connection**. Venice Forge refuses to store the key if Electron `safeStorage` encryption (DPAPI on Windows, Keychain on macOS) is unavailable.
   140	
   141	**Web mode:** copy `.env.example` to `.env` and set `VENICE_API_KEY`.
   142	
   143	### Optional Environment Variables
   144	
   145	| Variable | Purpose |
   146	|----------|---------|
   147	| `VENICE_FORGE_ALLOW_PLAINTEXT_KEY_STORAGE` | Allow plaintext fallback when OS secure storage is unavailable (Linux/non-GNOME only). **Warning:** reduces security. |
   148	| `VENICE_FORGE_DEBUG_DEVTOOLS` | Allow DevTools in packaged production builds. Only enable for debugging. |
   149	
   150	```
   151	VENICE_API_KEY="your-venice-inference-key"
   152	```
   153	
   154	## Storage
   155	
   156	| Data | Location |
   157	|------|----------|
   158	| API key | Electron `safeStorage` — Win: `%APPDATA%\Venice Forge\secure-prefs.json`<br>Mac: `~/Library/Application Support/Venice Forge/secure-prefs.json` |
   159	| Logs | Win: `%APPDATA%\Venice Forge\logs\venice-forge.log`<br>Mac: `~/Library/Application Support/Venice Forge/logs/venice-forge.log` |
   160	| Images, chats, settings | Renderer IndexedDB |
   161	| Exports | Versioned JSON with `version`, `exportedAt`, `appVersion`, and `data` |
   162	
   163	Import validates JSON size and schema, rejects unexpected stores, strips secret-like fields, and merges by ID rather than clearing existing data. API keys are never imported or exported. A backup of existing data is saved to disk before any import is applied.
   164	
   165	## Security Model
   166	
   167	Desktop Venice API calls go through a narrow preload API and main-process IPC transport. The renderer cannot read the raw API key, cannot invoke arbitrary IPC channels, and cannot choose arbitrary Venice endpoints. Allowed endpoints:
   168	
   169	- `GET /models`
   170	- `POST /chat/completions`
   171	- `POST /image/generate`
   172	- `POST /image/upscale`
   173	- `POST /augment/search`
   174	- `POST /augment/scrape`
   175	- `POST /augment/text-parser`
   176	
   177	Production CSP does not allow localhost networking. Navigation is blocked except for the app files; trusted external HTTPS links open in the OS browser. Packaged production DevTools are disabled unless `VENICE_FORGE_DEBUG_DEVTOOLS=true`. Web proxy mode adds `X-Content-Type-Options`, `X-Frame-Options`, `Referrer-Policy`, and `Content-Security-Policy` headers to all responses.
   178	
   179	Read our full [Privacy & Security Model](PRIVACY.md) and the technical [SECURITY.md](SECURITY.md) for more details.
   180	
   181	## Legal and Terms
   182	
   183	Venice Forge is an independent open-source client for the Venice API. It is not endorsed by, sponsored by, or affiliated with Venice.ai, Inc. Users are responsible for complying with the current [Venice Terms of Service](https://venice.ai/legal/tos), [Venice privacy information](https://venice.ai/privacy), and [Venice API documentation](https://docs.venice.ai/) when using their own API keys.
   184	
   185	See [docs/LEGAL.md](docs/LEGAL.md) for the public-readiness legal notes, trademark notice, privacy limits, and release disclaimers.
   186	
   187	## Troubleshooting
   188	
   189	| Symptom | Fix |
   190	|---------|-----|
   191	| Missing icon | `npm run generate:icon` then `npm run verify:icon` |
   192	| Packaging failure | `npm run clean && npm install && npm run dist:win` |
   193	| SmartScreen warning | Expected for unsigned local builds; see [docs/RELEASE/release.md](docs/RELEASE/release.md) for signing |
   194	| No API key prompt at launch | Open **Config**, save a key, then test connection |
   195	| `400` on chat/image | Usually a request schema mismatch — ensure the model ID is valid and all API parameters are correct strings |
   196	| `401` / `403` | Invalid key or insufficient key scope |
   197	| `429` | Venice rate limit; wait for the reset period shown in the Status tab |
   198	| Transport failure | Open **Status**, copy diagnostics, inspect the logs folder |
   199	
   200	## Known Limitations
   201	
   202	- Auto-updates are fetched securely via GitHub Releases.
   203	- Release signing is optional and not required for local builds.
   204	- IndexedDB records are encrypted with a browser-managed AES-GCM key stored in same-origin IndexedDB. This reduces casual local inspection risk but is not equivalent to OS credential storage and does not protect against malware, XSS, same-origin compromise, browser profile compromise, or a compromised OS user. Export before risky upgrades.
   205	- Malware running as the same OS user is out of scope and may access user data or process memory.
   206

   208

     1	# Repository Tree
     2	
     3	This document is the public map for the Venice Forge repository. It reflects the current dual-mode app layout: Electron desktop production mode and Express/Vite web development mode.
     4	
     5	## Top-Level Structure
     6	
     7	```text
     8	.

    18	│   │   └── windows-release.yml        # Windows build, NSIS setup/portable generation, checksums

    24	│   └── icon-placeholder.md

    90	## Runtime Segments
    91	
    92	| Segment | Path | Responsibility |
    93	|---------|------|----------------|
    94	| Renderer app | `src/` | React shell, tab modules, UI components, state, storage, import/export, Venice client facade |
    95	| Electron desktop | `electron/` | BrowserWindow, CSP, navigation guard, preload bridge, IPC handlers, safeStorage, HTTPS client |
    96	| Web proxy | `server.ts` | Local development Express server, Venice proxy, security headers, rate limiting, circuit breaker |
    97	| Shared validation | `src/shared/` | Venice endpoint and API host configuration shared by renderer, web proxy, and Electron IPC |
    98	| Build scripts | `scripts/` | CJS package marker generation and release artifact validation |
    99	| Release config | `electron-builder.config.cjs`, `.github/workflows/*-release.yml` | Windows and macOS application packaging |
   100	| Governance | `.github/`, `CONTRIBUTING.md`, `CODE_OF_CONDUCT.md`, `SECURITY.md`, `SUPPORT.md` | Public contribution, support, ownership, and automation metadata |
   101	
   102	## Source Organization
   103	
   104	| Path | Notes |
   105	|------|-------|
   106	| `src/modules/` | One file per app tab: chat, image generation, batch, research, models, gallery, settings, diagnostics |
   107	| `src/components/` | Reusable UI primitives and feature components |
   108	| `src/services/veniceClient.ts` | Only renderer entry point for Venice API calls |
   109	| `src/services/desktopBridge.ts` | Electron-vs-web transport abstraction |
   110	| `src/services/storageService.ts` | IndexedDB persistence for images, chats, settings, diagnostics |
   111	| `src/services/cryptoService.ts` | AES-GCM encryption for chats and settings |
   112	| `src/services/exportImport.ts` | Versioned JSON export/import with secret redaction |
   113	| `src/shared/validation.ts` | Allowed Venice endpoint and method list |
   114	| `electron/ipc/validation.ts` | Electron IPC request validation boundary |
   115	| `electron/services/secureStore.ts` | OS-encrypted API key persistence |
   116	| `electron/services/veniceClient.ts` | Main-process HTTPS client for `api.venice.ai` |
   117

     1	# Changelog
     2	
     3	All notable changes to this project will be documented in this file.
     4	
     5	Format follows [Keep a Changelog](https://keepachangelog.com/en/1.1.0/). Venice Forge uses [Semantic Versioning](https://semver.org/spec/v2.0.0.html).
     6	
     7	---
     8	
     9	## [Unreleased]
    10	
    11	### Added
    12	- Added dual-platform macOS + Windows packaging support.
    13	- Added generated macOS `.icns` application icon.
    14	- Added cross-platform checksum sidecar generation (`.sha256`) for distribution artifacts.
    15	- Added cross-platform local testing and release verification scripts.
    16	- Added macOS release workflow (`macos-release.yml`) for `arm64` and `x64` builds.
    17	- Added ESLint configuration (`eslint.config.mjs`) with TypeScript-ESLint and React Hooks rules.
    18	- Added Vitest coverage reporting via `@vitest/coverage-v8` and `npm run test:coverage`.
    19	- Added GitHub CodeQL security analysis workflow (`.github/workflows/codeql.yml`).
    20	- Added `npm run lint:eslint` script for static analysis.
    21	- Added README release ribbon and badges for CI, Windows release, latest GitHub release, license, Node support, TypeScript strict mode, Electron, and Venice API.
    22	- Added `docs/REPOSITORY_TREE.md` with a public repository map and segment ownership notes.
    23	- Added `docs/LEGAL.md` with Venice.ai TOS/privacy/API links, affiliation notice, API key handling notes, and release disclaimers.
    24	- Added root `SECURITY.md`, `SUPPORT.md`, GitHub issue templates, pull request template, and Dependabot configuration.
    25	- Added `docs/Venice_swagger_api.yaml` and `docs/venice_llm_info.md` as the canonical API reference used for alignment work.
    26	
    27	### Changed
    28	- Refactored `verify-dist` to support both Windows and macOS file validations.
    29	- `secureStore.ts` strictly enforces macOS Keychain encryption exactly like Windows DPAPI.
    30	- Updated all supporting documentation to match the current app status and public release process.
    31	- CI workflow now uses `npm ci --prefer-offline` for slightly faster installs and reproducibility.
    32	- Windows release workflow now generates and uploads SHA-256 checksum sidecar files for `.exe` artifacts.
    33	- Updated `metadata.json` to describe Venice Forge instead of the previous empty/generated metadata.
    34	- `readDesktopErrorBody` (`src/services/veniceClient.ts`) and `readResponseError` (`electron/services/veniceClient.ts`) both now correctly parse Venice `DetailedError` (Zod format: `{ details: { _errors, fieldName: { _errors } } }`) — previously fell through to "Unknown Venice API error" for all schema-validation failures.
    35	- Diagnostic dispatch deduplication: failed Venice requests now emit exactly one `SET_DIAGNOSTICS` entry with the resolved error message. Previously, each failure emitted two entries — an initial empty-error entry and a second entry with the error — causing duplicate rows in the Status log.
    36	- Web-mode diagnostics parity: non-2xx responses in the web transport now parse Venice `DetailedError` consistently and avoid catch-path duplicate diagnostics once an HTTP diagnostics entry has already been emitted.
    37	
    38	### Fixed
    39	- **CI:** `.github/workflows/windows-release.yml` referenced non-existent `actions/checkout@v6` and `actions/setup-node@v6`. Downgraded to `@v4` to match the latest published action versions and restore the release pipeline.
    40	- **Test:** `src/services/desktopBridge.test.ts` failed with `ReferenceError: indexedDB is not defined` because `vi.stubGlobal("window", {})` stripped the fake-indexeddb instance from jsdom. The test now stubs `window` with `{ indexedDB: global.indexedDB }` so the `isConfigured()` path can open the fake database.
    41	- **BUG-003:** Settings auto-save had no debounce — rapid changes could race and persist out-of-order state. Added a 500 ms debounce to the save effect.
    42	- **BUG-004:** IndexedDB init failure still marked `dbReady=true`, causing later writes to a broken database. Only sets `dbReady`/`settingsHydrated` on successful init.
    43	- **BUG-005:** `SET_CHAT_DRAFT`, `SET_IMAGE_DRAFT`, `SET_BATCH_DRAFT` reducers crashed on `null`/`undefined` patch. Added truthy guard before `Object.assign`.
    44	- **BUG-006:** `dedupeKey` threw unhandled `TypeError` on circular request bodies. Wrapped `JSON.stringify` in try/catch with `"[circular]"` fallback.
    45	- **BUG-007:** Import loops over stores sequentially with `await` inside `for…of`. Store writes are now parallelised via `Promise.all`.
    46	- **BUG-008:** Rate-limit `reqCounts` Map grew unbounded under multi-IP traffic. Added a 10,000-entry cap with FIFO eviction.
    47	- **BUG-010:** Raw `console.error`/`console.warn` calls left in production renderer and server paths (17 occurrences). Replaced with conditional shared logger (`src/shared/logger.ts`).
    48	- **BUG-011:** `AbortSignal.any`/`AbortSignal.timeout` may throw in older runtimes. Added `createTimeoutSignal()` helper with manual fallback.
    49	- **BUG-013:** `veniceFetch` deduplication map could leak promises on abrupt navigation. Added `beforeunload` listener that clears `inFlight`.
    50	- **BUG-018:** `veniceFetchDesktop` asserted `method as "GET" | "POST"` instead of narrowing. Method parameter now typed as `"GET" | "POST"`.
    51	- **BUG-019:** `veniceFetch<T = any>` disabled TypeScript inference. Generic default changed from `any` to `unknown`.
    52	- **BUG-022:** Log rotation overwrote the single backup file. Implemented 3-file rotation ring (`.1`, `.2`, `.3`).
    53	- **BUG-023:** `catch (err: any)` used in 8+ production files — loose error typing masked safety. Replaced with `catch (err)` and runtime guards (`err instanceof Error`).
    54	- **BUG-028:** `sleep` ignored already-aborted signals, allowing stale timeouts to proceed. Now rejects immediately if `signal.aborted` before setting timeout.
    55	- **BUG-029:** `modelService` swallowed `localStorage` write failures silently. Empty catch now warns via shared logger.
    56	- **BUG-030:** `byteLength` used `new Blob([value]).size` — slow for large strings. Replaced with `new TextEncoder().encode(value).length`.
    57	- **BUG-036:** `SettingsModuleProps` used `state: any, dispatch: any`. Now typed with `AppState` and `AppDispatch`.
    58	- **BUG-037:** `desktopUpdates` callbacks typed as `(info: unknown)` / `(progress: unknown)`. Now use `UpdateInfo` and `ProgressInfo` from `electron-updater`.
    59	- **BUG-040:** `normalizeWebSearchSetting` did not warn on invalid input. Now logs a warning when coercion happens.
    60	- **BUG-042:** `isAllowedAppNavigation` used `path.normalize` without symlink resolution. Added `fs.realpathSync` with try/catch for both target and root paths.
    61	- **BUG-043:** `verify-dist-mac.cjs` artifact name pattern did not match `electron-builder` default zip naming. Added `zip.artifactName` to `electron-builder.config.cjs` to align naming.
    62	- **BUG-044:** `BatchDraft` interface had wrong fields (`prompts`, `model`, `systemPrompt` instead of `promptsText`). Fixed type to match actual runtime state; removed inline cast in `BatchModule`.
    63	- **BUG-045:** `cryptoService.keyPromise` rejection was never cleared, causing permanent cache miss on any key-init failure. Added `.catch` handler to reset latch and allow retry.
    64	- **BUG-046:** IPC `endpoint.search` query string was forwarded without length cap, allowing pathological renderer inputs. Added 512-byte limit before building the return value.
    65	- **BUG-047:** Web-mode export `URL.revokeObjectURL` was called synchronously after `a.click()`, causing race where download failed before browser processed the blob. Deferred revocation by 1 second.
    66	- **BUG-048:** Circuit breaker `circuitFailures` counter never reset when `circuitOpenUntil` timeout expired. Half-open reset now clears both `circuitFailures` and `circuitOpenUntil` on recovery window re-entry.
    67	- **BUG-049:** `setInterval` for rate-limit map cleanup leaked on each `createServerApp()` call in tests. Stored interval ID and exposed `cleanupIntervals()` method on returned `app` object.
    68	- **BUG-050:** `AppSettings.apiKey` field declared in type but never written by `SET_SETTINGS` reducer, leading to misleading type surface. Removed unused field.
    69	- **BUG-021:** `StorageService` and `cryptoService` exposed `any` in public APIs (4 occurrences). Added `EncryptedPayload` and `KeyRecord` types; replaced `any` with proper generics in `getOrCreateKey`, `encryptData<T>`, `decryptData<T>`, and sort comparator.
    70	- **DOC-012:** `.env.example` labeled `VENICE_TIMEOUT_MS` as "legacy fallback" but code still actively reads it. Updated comment to "Deprecated alias for VENICE_API_TIMEOUT_MS — still accepted as fallback".
    71	- **BUG-004 (payload):** `enable_web_search` was serialised as a boolean (`true`/`false`) instead of the required string enum (`"auto"` / `"on"` / `"off"`), causing HTTP 400 on every `/chat/completions` request. `buildChatPayload` now passes the string value directly (defaulting to `"off"`).
    72	- **BUG-005 (payload):** Venice `DetailedError` responses (Zod validation failures) were not parsed — the error body contains a `details` object with `_errors` arrays and no top-level `error` field. Both the renderer and Electron main-process clients now extract the first `_errors` message or a field-level error when present.
    73	- **BUG-006 (payload):** Every failed Venice request produced two entries in the diagnostics log: one with `error: ""` from the initial HTTP dispatch, and a second with the actual message from the retry/catch path. The redundant dispatch has been removed; the initial entry now carries the fully resolved error.
    74	- **BUG-007 (payload):** Legacy persisted settings could still carry boolean `webSearch` values (`true`/`false`), which mapped to invalid API payloads and recurring `400` schema errors. Settings ingestion now coerces legacy values to `on`/`off`/`auto`, and chat payload construction enforces the same normalization.
    75	- **BUG-008 (payload):** Desktop `/augment/text-parser` uploads were unstable because `veniceFetchDesktop` serialized `FormData` but still sent the raw body over IPC. The request now correctly sends the serialized multipart payload, restoring reliable file-upload request construction.
    76	
    77	### Security
    78	- Explicitly disabled plaintext API-key fallback on macOS.
    79	- Documented web proxy forbidden-header stripping and proxy-root rejection.
    80	- Added Venice.ai TOS, privacy, and API documentation coverage for public releases.
    81	
    82	---
    83	
    84	## [1.0.1] — 2026-05-20
    85	
    86	### Security
    87	- **SEC-001:** Added `/augment/search`, `/augment/scrape`, `/augment/text-parser` to the IPC and web-proxy endpoint allowlist. These endpoints were previously blocked, making the Research tab non-functional in both Electron and web modes.
    88	- **SEC-002:** Added `safeHref()` sanitization to search result anchor tags. Only `http:` and `https:` scheme URLs are allowed; `javascript:`, `data:`, and other schemes are replaced with `#` to prevent XSS.
    89	- **SEC-003 (web proxy):** Added security response headers — `X-Content-Type-Options: nosniff`, `X-Frame-Options: DENY`, `Referrer-Policy: no-referrer`, and `Content-Security-Policy` — to all web-proxy responses.
    90	
    91	### Fixed
    92	- **BUG-001:** `galleryFilename` was called with a plain string instead of the item object in bulk gallery download, producing `venice-undefined-undefined.png` filenames for all downloads.
    93	- **BUG-002:** Import backup was constructed in memory but never written to disk before import records were applied, misleading the user with a "backup prepared" message.
    94	- **BUG-003:** Removed dead `const endedAt = nowIso()` variable captured before `fetch()` was called in `veniceClient.ts`.
    95	
    96	### Changed
    97	- `upscaleGalleryImage` now accepts a `model` parameter (default `"upscale-model"`); `GalleryModule` passes `state.selectedImageModel` so the currently selected model is used.
    98	- Express `trust proxy` is configurable through `TRUST_PROXY`; removed deprecated `req.connection.remoteAddress` fallback so rate limiting uses the correct client IP behind a configured reverse proxy.
    99	- Excluded `vite.config.ts` and test files from `tsconfig.json`; `npm run typecheck` now exits with zero errors.
   100	
   101	### Added
   102	- 25 new tests across `server.test.ts`, `src/utils/image.test.ts`, `src/utils/markdown.test.ts` — total 41 tests (was 16). Coverage includes: augment endpoint validation, rate limiter enforcement, security header assertions, `galleryFilename` regression guard, `normalizeImageData`, `extractImages`, markdown XSS safety, and `escapeHtml`.
   103

   105	
   106	## [1.0.0] — 2026-05-20
   107	
   108	### Added
   109	
   110	**Core features**
   111	- Dual-mode application: Electron desktop (Windows) and Vite/Express web development mode.
   112	- **Prompt tab:** Streaming chat completions with system-prompt control, model selection, stop/abort, and conversation history stored in IndexedDB.
   113	- **Create tab:** Single and batch image generation with configurable dimensions, steps, guidance scale, negative prompt, seed, and watermark control. One-click upscaling via Venice upscale endpoint. Images saved to local gallery.
   114	- **Batch tab:** Run one prompt across multiple inputs, or run many prompts in sequence, with live progress, abort, and per-result download.
   115	- **Research tab:** Venice-augmented web search (Brave and Google providers), page scraping, and document text extraction via Venice augment endpoints.
   116	- **Catalog tab:** Live Venice model browser showing model ID, type, traits, and capabilities; falls back to built-in model list on network error.
   117	- **Library tab:** Local image gallery with individual download, upscale, delete, and bulk-download (up to 50 images at a time).
   118	- **Config tab:** API key save/test/delete (desktop), theme selection, image/chat model defaults, JSON data import/export with schema validation and ID-merge (not overwrite).
   119	- **Status tab:** Diagnostics panel showing transport mode, runtime/app versions, storage info, API key state, rate-limit headers, and one-click log folder access.
   120	
   121	**Architecture and security**
   122	- Electron main process with strict IPC validation (`validateVeniceIpcRequest`), sandboxed renderer, context isolation, and preload bridge (`window.veniceForge`).
   123	- API key stored via Electron `safeStorage`; plaintext fallback disabled unless `VENICE_FORGE_ALLOW_PLAINTEXT_KEY_STORAGE=true`.
   124	- Restrictive production CSP; navigation blocked to non-app URLs; external HTTPS links open in OS browser.
   125	- Express web proxy with endpoint allowlist, method validation, rate limiting, circuit breaker, and `express.raw` body passthrough.
   126	- Log redaction for authorization headers, API keys, bearer tokens, and secret-like field values.
   127	- Versioned JSON export/import with size validation, store validation, and secret field stripping.
   128	
   129	**Developer experience**
   130	- TypeScript strict mode throughout renderer and Electron main.
   131	- Vitest test suite with supertest integration tests for the Express proxy.
   132	- CI matrix (Node 20 + 22) via GitHub Actions.
   133	- Windows release workflow with NSIS installer and portable exe, upload to GitHub Releases.
   134	- Placeholder icon generation and verification scripts.
   135	- `npm run clean`, `npm run typecheck`, `npm run verify:dist` convenience scripts.
   136	- `.env.example` with all configurable environment variables documented.

<!-- call_id: tool_pFLViU3t3rYCYgzWc1hvk25V -->
<system>116 lines read from file starting from line 1. Total lines in file: 116. End of file reached.</system>
     1	# About Venice Forge
     2	
     3	## What Is Venice Forge?
     4	
     5	Venice Forge is a **private AI creation studio** built as a dual-platform Windows and macOS Electron desktop application. It provides a unified interface for the [Venice API](https://venice.ai), covering text generation, image generation, web research, batch automation, and local data management — all without routing user content through any intermediary server beyond Venice itself.
     6	
     7	The project ships as a packaged Electron desktop app for Windows and macOS, plus a Vite/Express web application for local development.
     8	
     9	Current public readiness status:
    10	
    11	- Source is MIT licensed and suitable for public repository browsing.
    12	- CI runs lint, typecheck, tests, and build on Node 20 and 22.
    13	- Release automation builds Windows NSIS/portable `.exe` artifacts and macOS DMG/ZIP artifacts.
    14	- Root support, security, contribution, code of conduct, issue template, PR template, and Dependabot metadata are present.
    15	- Legal/TOS notes are maintained in [LEGAL.md](LEGAL.md).
    16	- FAQ and troubleshooting guides are maintained in [FAQ.md](FAQ.md) and [TROUBLESHOOTING.md](TROUBLESHOOTING.md).
    17	
    18	## Goals
    19	
    20	- **Privacy by default.** The Venice API is privacy-preserving by design. Venice Forge keeps API keys out of the renderer process, never persists keys in plaintext, and never exports them.
    21	- **Offline-first storage.** Images, chat history, and settings live in browser IndexedDB — no cloud sync, no telemetry.
    22	- **Practical security.** The Electron architecture enforces strict IPC validation, a narrow preload surface, and a restrictive CSP. The web proxy enforces the same endpoint allowlist plus rate limiting and security headers.
    23	- **Reproducible builds.** TypeScript strict mode, a CI matrix across Node 20 and 22, and `npm ci` ensure every build starts from a known state.
    24	
    25	## Architecture
    26	
    27	```
    28	┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
    29	│  Electron Process Boundary                                 │
    30	│                                                            │
    31	│  ┌─────────────────────┐        ┌──────────────────────┐  │
    32	│  │  Renderer (React)   │  IPC   │  Main Process        │  │
    33	│  │  - No Node.js       │◄──────►│  - venice HTTPS      │  │
    34	│  │  - Sandbox enabled  │        │  - safeStorage       │  │
    35	│  │  - Context isolated │        │  - Logger            │  │
    36	│  │  - window.venice    │        │  - IPC validation    │  │
    37	│  │    Forge bridge     │        │  - OS dialogs        │  │
    38	│  └─────────────────────┘        └──────────────────────┘  │
    39	│                                          │                 │
    40	│                                          ▼                 │
    41	│                                  api.venice.ai (HTTPS)     │
    42	└────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
    43	
    44	Web mode (development only):
    45	  Browser → Vite dev server → Express /api/venice → api.venice.ai
    46	```
    47	
    48	### Key Layers
    49	
    50	| Layer | Technology | Responsibility |
    51	|-------|-----------|----------------|
    52	| UI | React 19 + Tailwind v4 | All user-facing screens |
    53	| State | useReducer + Immer | Centralised app state |
    54	| Storage | IndexedDB (via `StorageService`) | Images, chats, settings |
    55	| Secure storage | Electron `safeStorage` | API key (encrypted) |
    56	| IPC bridge | Electron preload + `ipcMain` | Renderer ↔ main transport |
    57	| Web proxy | Express + http-proxy-middleware | Dev/web mode proxy |
    58	| Packaging | electron-builder | Windows NSIS/portable, macOS DMG/ZIP |
    59	| Automation | GitHub Actions + Dependabot | CI, Windows/macOS release, dependency updates |
    60	| QA | Vitest + ESLint (`--max-warnings=96`) | Unit tests, integration tests, static analysis |
    61	
    62	### Application Tabs
    63	
    64	| Tab | Feature |
    65	|-----|---------|
    66	| Prompt | Streaming chat with Venice text models |
    67	| Create | Image generation with upscaling and gallery save |
    68	| Batch | Sequential prompt runs over multiple inputs |
    69	| Research | Web search, page scrape, and document parse via Venice augment endpoints |
    70	| Catalog | Live model browser (type, traits, capability) |
    71	| Library | Local image gallery with bulk download and upscale |
    72	| Config | API key management, theme selection, import/export |
    73	| Status | Diagnostics, rate-limit info, log access |
    74	
    75	## Technology Stack
    76	
    77	- **Frontend:** React 19, TypeScript strict, Tailwind CSS v4, Vite 6
    78	- **Desktop:** Electron 42, electron-builder 26 (Windows NSIS + portable)
    79	- **Backend (web mode):** Express 4, http-proxy-middleware 4, dotenv
    80	- **State:** React `useReducer` with Immer for immutable updates
    81	- **Testing:** Vitest 4, @testing-library/react, supertest
    82	- **Build:** esbuild (Electron main), Vite (renderer), tsc (type checking)
    83	
    84	## Data Flow
    85	
    86	```
    87	User input
    88	  └─► React component
    89	        └─► veniceFetch() / desktopBridge IPC
    90	              ├─ Electron: main process validates → HTTPS → api.venice.ai
    91	              └─ Web:      Express /api/venice → HTTPS → api.venice.ai
    92	                                        ↓
    93	                               Response data
    94	                                        ↓
    95	                            IndexedDB (images / chats)
    96	                                        ↓
    97	                            React state update → UI
    98	```
    99	
   100	## Non-Goals
   101	
   102	- Venice Forge auto-update support depends on GitHub Releases availability and packaging configuration.
   103	- IndexedDB records are encrypted with a browser-managed AES-GCM key stored in same-origin IndexedDB; this is not equivalent to OS credential storage.
   104	- Venice Forge is not a multi-user or server-deployed application; it is a single-user desktop tool.
   105	- Venice Forge does not support Linux native packaging in the current release.
   106	- Venice Forge is not an official Venice.ai product and does not replace Venice's legal terms, privacy notices, or API documentation.
   107	
   108	## Further Reading
   109	
   110	- [README.md](../README.md) — Setup and usage
   111	- [docs/SECURITY.md](../SECURITY.md) — Full security model
   112	- [docs/RELEASE.md](RELEASE/release.md) — Release and signing process
   113	- [docs/LEGAL.md](LEGAL.md) — Legal and Venice terms coverage
   114	- [docs/REPOSITORY_TREE.md](REPOSITORY_TREE.md) — Repository structure
   115	- [CONTRIBUTING.md](../CONTRIBUTING.md) — How to contribute
   116	- [CHANGELOG.md](../CHANGELOG.md) — Version history


</details>

     1	# Venice Forge — Frequently Asked Questions
     2	
     3	## General
     4	
     5	### What is Venice Forge?
     6	Venice Forge is an independent, open-source desktop client for the [Venice API](https://venice.ai). It provides a unified interface for text generation, image generation, web research, batch automation, and local data management — all without routing user content through any intermediary server beyond Venice itself.
     7	
     8	### Is Venice Forge an official Venice.ai product?
     9	No. Venice Forge is an independent MIT-licensed project. It is not endorsed by, sponsored by, or affiliated with Venice.ai, Inc. "Venice", "Venice.ai", and related marks belong to their respective owners.
    10	
    11	### What platforms are supported?
    12	- **Windows 10/11** (x64) — NSIS installer and portable `.exe`
    13	- **macOS 13+** (Apple Silicon `arm64` and Intel `x64`) — DMG and ZIP
    14	- **Linux** — Not officially packaged; development use only with plaintext key fallback
    15	- **Web browser** — Supported in development mode only
    16	
    17	See [PLATFORM_SUPPORT.md](DEVELOPMENT/platform-support.md) for the full matrix.
    18	
    19	---
    20	
    21	## Development & Building
    22	
    23	### What Node.js version do I need?
    24	Node.js **20 or 22** with npm 10+. The CI matrix tests both versions.
    25	
    26	### How do I start development?
    27	```bash
    28	npm install
    29	npm run dev:electron   # Desktop mode (recommended)
    30	# or
    31	npm run dev:web        # Web proxy mode
    32	```
    33	
    34	### What is the full validation gate?
    35	```bash
    36	npm run lint:eslint    # ESLint with --max-warnings=96
    37	npm run typecheck      # TypeScript for renderer + Electron
    38	npm test               # Vitest unit and integration tests
    39	npm run build          # Build dist/ and dist-electron/
    40	```
    41	
    42	### Why does `npm run lint:eslint` fail?
    43	The project enforces a warning budget of **96**. Common causes:
    44	- Using `any` instead of narrow types — replace with `unknown` + runtime guards.
    45	- Unused variables — prefix intentionally unused parameters with `_`.
    46	
    47	### Why are `dev` and `dev:web` the same command?
    48	Both run `tsx server.ts` (the Express web proxy). `dev:web` is the explicit alias used throughout documentation. `dev` is the shorthand default.
    49	
    50	---
    51	
    52	## API Keys & Security
    53	
    54	### Where is my API key stored?
    55	- **Desktop mode:** Encrypted with OS-level secure storage — DPAPI on Windows, Keychain on macOS. Never exposed to the renderer.
    56	- **Web mode:** In the server's `.env` file; never sent to the browser.
    57	
    58	### What if secure storage is unavailable?
    59	On macOS and Windows, the app **refuses** to store the key if secure storage fails. On Linux, you can set `VENICE_FORGE_ALLOW_PLAINTEXT_KEY_STORAGE=true` in `.env` to allow a documented plaintext fallback. **This reduces security.**
    60	
    61	### How do I enable DevTools in a production build?
    62	Set `VENICE_FORGE_DEBUG_DEVTOOLS=true` in your environment before launching. Only use this for debugging.
    63	
    64	### Is there telemetry?
    65	No. Venice Forge does not track users, log prompts, or monitor API key usage.
    66	
    67	---
    68	
    69	## Packaging & Releases
    70	
    71	### How do I build for Windows?
    72	```bash
    73	npm run dist:win
    74	npm run checksum:release
    75	npm run verify:dist:win
    76	npm run verify:dist:portable
    77	```
    78	
    79	### How do I build for macOS?
    80	```bash
    81	npm run dist:mac
    82	npm run checksum:release
    83	npm run verify:dist:mac
    84	```
    85	
    86	### What artifacts are generated?
    87	- Windows: `Venice-Forge-<version>-x64-Setup.exe`, `Venice-Forge-<version>-x64-Portable.exe`
    88	- macOS: `Venice-Forge-<version>-<arch>.dmg`, `Venice-Forge-<version>-<arch>.zip`
    89	- All artifacts include `.sha256` checksum sidecars.
    90	
    91	### Why does macOS Gatekeeper block my build?
    92	Local builds are ad-hoc signed without an Apple Developer ID certificate. For your own locally trusted builds:
    93	```bash
    94	xattr -dr com.apple.quarantine "/Applications/Venice Forge.app"
    95	```
    96	**Never use this for untrusted or internet-downloaded binaries.**
    97	
    98	---
    99	
   100	## Data & Storage
   101	
   102	### Where is my data stored?
   103	- **Images, chats, settings:** Renderer IndexedDB (local only).
   104	- **API key:** OS secure storage (Windows DPAPI / macOS Keychain).
   105	- **Logs:**
   106	  - Windows: `%APPDATA%\Venice Forge\logs\venice-forge.log`
   107	  - macOS: `~/Library/Application Support/Venice Forge/logs/venice-forge.log`
   108	
   109	### Is my data encrypted?
   110	Chats and settings are encrypted with AES-GCM using a browser-managed key stored in same-origin IndexedDB. This reduces casual local inspection risk but is **not equivalent to OS credential storage**.
   111	
   112	### Can I export my data?
   113	Yes. Use the **Config** tab → **Export**. Exports are versioned JSON with `version`, `exportedAt`, `appVersion`, and `data`. API keys are automatically redacted.
   114	
   115	### Can I import data?
   116	Yes. Use the **Config** tab → **Import**. Import validates JSON size and schema, rejects unexpected stores, strips secret-like fields, and merges by ID rather than clearing existing data. A pre-import backup is saved to disk.
   117	
   118	---
   119	
   120	## Troubleshooting
   121	
   122	### I get a 400 error on chat/image generation
   123	Usually a request schema mismatch. Ensure:
   124	- The model ID is valid.
   125	- `webSearch` is `"off"`, `"on"`, or `"auto"` (not a boolean).
   126	- All API parameters are correct strings.
   127	
   128	### I get a 401/403 error
   129	Your API key is invalid, expired, or has insufficient scope. Check the **Status** tab for diagnostics.
   130	
   131	### I get a 429 error
   132	Venice rate limit exceeded. Wait for the reset period shown in the **Status** tab.
   133	
   134	### The app crashes on startup
   135	Check the logs folder (see Data & Storage above). Common causes:
   136	- Missing icons: run `npm run generate:icon`.
   137	- Secure storage unavailable: ensure your OS key manager is functioning.
   138	- Corrupted IndexedDB: clear site data for the app.
   139	
   140	---
   141	
   142	## Contributing
   143	
   144	### How do I report a bug?
   145	Open a GitHub issue using the bug report template. Include:
   146	- App version from `package.json` or the Status tab.
   147	- Runtime mode (Electron desktop or web mode).
   148	- OS, Node.js version, and CPU architecture.
   149	- Steps to reproduce.
   150	- Sanitized diagnostics from the Status tab.
   151	
   152	### How do I report a security vulnerability?
   153	**Do not open a public issue.** Follow [SECURITY.md](../SECURITY.md) and request a private maintainer discussion.
   154	
   155	### What is the code style?
   156	- TypeScript **strict mode**.
   157	- Avoid `any`; use proper types or `unknown` + guards.
   158	- Use `function` declarations for modules.
   159	- Tailwind v4 utility classes inline with JSX.
   160	
   161	---
   162	
   163	## Further Reading
   164	
   165	- [README.md](../README.md) — Setup and usage
   166	- [ABOUT.md](ABOUT.md) — Architecture and goals
   167	- [BUILDING.md](DEVELOPMENT/building.md) — Development and packaging commands
   168	- [RELEASE.md](RELEASE/release.md) — Release checklist
   169	- [SECURITY.md](../SECURITY.md) — Full security model
   170	- [LEGAL.md](LEGAL.md) — Legal and TOS coverage

     1	# Building Venice Forge
     2	
     3	This document covers all commands for local development, packaging, and validation across Windows and macOS.
     4	
     5	## Quick Start (Development)
     6	
     7	```bash
     8	npm install
     9	npm run dev:electron   # Start the desktop app in development mode
    10	# or
    11	npm run dev:web        # Start the web proxy development mode
    12	```
    13	
    14	## Cross-Platform Validation
    15	
    16	Before submitting a PR, always run the cross-platform baseline validations:
    17	```bash
    18	npm run lint:eslint
    19	npm run typecheck
    20	npm test
    21	npm run build
    22	npm run verify:icon
    23	```
    24	
    25	## Packaging for Windows
    26	
    27	Run the following on Windows PowerShell:
    28	```powershell
    29	npm run dist:win
    30	npm run checksum:release
    31	npm run verify:dist:win
    32	npm run verify:dist:portable
    33	```
    34	
    35	This generates NSIS setup executables and portable binaries in the `release/` directory.
    36	
    37	## Packaging for macOS
    38	
    39	Run the following on macOS Terminal:
    40	```bash
    41	npm run dist:mac
    42	npm run checksum:release
    43	npm run verify:dist:mac
    44	```
    45	
    46	This generates Apple Silicon and Intel `.dmg` and `.zip` artifacts in the `release/` directory.
    47	
    48	## Checksums
    49	The `npm run checksum:release` script runs deterministically across platforms, outputting a `<filename>.sha256` sidecar for every `.exe`, `.dmg`, and `.zip` artifact.

<system>46 lines read from file starting from line 1. Total lines in file: 46. End of file reached.</system>
     1	# Troubleshooting
     2	
     3	## Packaging and Build Failures
     4	
     5	**Missing Icons**
     6	Error: `Missing build/icon.ico` or `Missing build/icon.icns`
     7	Solution: Run `npm run generate:icon` to rebuild the placeholders.
     8	
     9	**SafeStorage Unavailable**
    10	Error: `macOS secure storage is unavailable` or `Windows secure storage is unavailable`.
    11	Solution: The app refuses to store the API key in plaintext. Ensure your OS key manager (DPAPI or Keychain) is functioning. For macOS, this may fail if you are running in a headless CI runner without a keychain unlocked.
    12	
    13	## OS Security Warnings
    14	
    15	**macOS Gatekeeper**
    16	Error: "Venice Forge cannot be opened because the developer cannot be verified."
    17	Solution: For local builds only, you can strip the quarantine flag:
    18	```bash
    19	xattr -dr com.apple.quarantine "/Applications/Venice Forge.app"
    20	```
    21	
    22	**Windows SmartScreen**
    23	Error: "Windows protected your PC."
    24	Solution: Click "More info" and then "Run anyway" for locally built unsigned binaries.
    25	
    26	## Runtime Issues
    27	
    28	**Invalid Venice Key / Rate Limits**
    29	Check the **Status** tab for the latest sanitized API error. If you receive continuous 400 or 401 errors, your key is likely expired or malformed.
    30	Logs are available at:
    31	- **Windows**: `%APPDATA%\Venice Forge\logs\venice-forge.log`
    32	- **macOS**: `~/Library/Application Support/Venice Forge/logs/venice-forge.log`
    33	
    34	**Lint Gate Failures (`npm run lint:eslint`)**
    35	The project enforces `--max-warnings=96`. If you see `✖ N problems (0 errors, N warnings)` where `N > 96`, reduce warnings before committing. Common sources:
    36	- `@typescript-eslint/no-explicit-any` — replace `any` with a narrow type or `unknown` + runtime guard.
    37	- `@typescript-eslint/no-unused-vars` — prefix intentionally unused args with `_`.
    38	
    39	**Type-Check Failures (`npm run typecheck`)**
    40	Both `tsconfig.json` (renderer) and `tsconfig.electron.json` (main) must pass. If Electron-only code fails, run `npx tsc --noEmit --project tsconfig.electron.json` to isolate errors.
    41	
    42	**Portable Build Verification Fails**
    43	If `npm run verify:dist:portable` reports a missing executable, confirm:
    44	1. `npm run dist:portable` completed without errors.
    45	2. The artifact exists in `release/Venice-Forge-<version>-x64-Portable.exe`.
    46	3. The `.sha256` sidecar was generated by `npm run checksum:release`.


</details>

     1	# Signing and Notarization
     2	
     3	Public distribution of Electron applications requires OS-level code signing to bypass security warnings.
     4	
     5	> **Note**: Local builds executed via `npm run dist:win` or `npm run dist:mac` are unsigned by default. Unsigned builds will trigger Windows SmartScreen and macOS Gatekeeper warnings.
     6	
     7	## Windows Authenticode
     8	
     9	Windows requires an EV or Standard Code Signing Certificate to clear SmartScreen warnings.
    10	`electron-builder` requires the following environment variables:
    11	- `WIN_CSC_LINK`: Path or URL to the certificate.
    12	- `WIN_CSC_KEY_PASSWORD`: Password for the certificate.
    13	
    14	## macOS Developer ID and Notarization
    15	
    16	Apple requires both application signing and automated Notarization.
    17	`electron-builder` will attempt to sign and notarize the app if the following are provided:
    18	- `CSC_LINK` / `CSC_KEY_PASSWORD`: P12 certificate and password.
    19	- Apple App Store Connect credentials (usually configured via `APPLE_ID` and `APPLE_APP_SPECIFIC_PASSWORD`).
    20	
    21	For our local builds, `hardenedRuntime: true` is enabled in `electron-builder.config.cjs`. Unsigned local binaries will still successfully build; the hardened runtime flag primarily affects notarization requirements for public releases. 
    22	
    23	**Never commit code signing certificates or passwords to the repository.**


</details>

     1	# Venice Forge — Agent Entry Guide
     2	
     3	This is the token-lean entrypoint. Read [`AGENT_REINITIALIZATION.md`](./AGENT_REINITIALIZATION.md) first for full current context.
     4	
     5	## Primary Rules
     6	
     7	1. Protect security boundaries first.
     8	2. Keep renderer/main/web-mode contracts aligned.
     9	3. Prefer narrow, test-backed changes in high-churn files.
    10	4. Never assume architecture history; verify in git.
    11	
    12	## Startup Checklist (Always)
    13	
    14	1. Open `AGENT_REINITIALIZATION.md` and scan:
    15	   - architecture model,
    16	   - recent change table,
    17	   - pitfalls,
    18	   - commands/CI.
    19	2. Confirm current scripts in `package.json`.
    20	3. Confirm current workflows in `.github/workflows/`.
    21	4. If changing transport/security, read first:
    22	   - `src/services/veniceClient.ts`
    23	   - `server.ts`
    24	   - `electron/ipc/validation.ts`
    25	   - `electron/ipc/handlers.ts`
    26	   - `electron/main.ts`
    27	
    28	## Non-Negotiable Boundaries
    29	
    30	- Renderer API traffic goes through `src/services/veniceClient.ts`.
    31	- Electron renderer must stay sandboxed (`contextIsolation: true`, `nodeIntegration: false`, `sandbox: true`).
    32	- Venice endpoint/method allowlist must stay synced across:
    33	  - `src/shared/validation.ts`
    34	  - `electron/ipc/validation.ts`
    35	  - `server.ts`
    36	- New IPC surface requires coordinated updates:
    37	  - `electron/preload.ts`
    38	  - `electron/ipc/handlers.ts`
    39	  - validation path
    40	  - renderer bridge/types/tests
    41	
    42	## Current Operational Reality
    43	
    44	- Dual mode exists:
    45	  - Electron direct IPC transport.
    46	  - Web proxy transport (`/api/venice/*`).
    47	- Release targets are Windows + macOS.
    48	- ESLint gate exists locally (`npm run lint:eslint`) with `--max-warnings=96`.
    49	- GitHub `ci.yml` runs lint:eslint, typecheck, test, and build.
    50	
    51	## Coding Expectations
    52	
    53	- Keep edits scoped; avoid mixed restyle + logic + security diffs in one patch.
    54	- Add regression tests for bug fixes (`BUG-###` comment convention when applicable).
    55	- Preserve decrypt-failure warning behavior in storage flows.
    56	- Reuse shared limits/constants instead of hardcoding bytes or endpoint lists.
    57	
    58	## Quick Commands
    59	
    60	```bash
    61	npm run dev:electron
    62	npm run dev:web
    63	npm run typecheck
    64	npm run lint:eslint
    65	npm test
    66	npm run build
    67	```
    68	
    69	Release and verification commands are documented in `AGENT_REINITIALIZATION.md`.
    70	
    71	## When You Must Refresh Context
    72	
    73	Refresh `AGENT_REINITIALIZATION.md` after:
    74	
    75	- architecture or transport boundary changes,
    76	- workflow/script changes,
    77	- shared validation/limits changes,
    78	- major refactors in high-churn modules.
    79	
    80	Use git-grounded evidence only; if unknown, write:
    81	
    82	`UNKNOWN — not inferable from repo`
